tree is used for incremental sorting of data.\\n106: /// The table consists of several sorted parts.\\n107: /// During insertion new data is sorted according to the primary key and is written to the new part.\\n108: /// Parts are merged in the background according to a heuristic algorithm.\\n109: /// For each part the index file is created containing primary key values for every n-th row.\\n110: /// This allows efficient selection by primary key range predicate.\\n111: ///\\n112: /// Additionally:\\n113: ///\\n114: /// The date column is specified. For each part min and max dates are remembered.\\n115: /// Essentially it is an index too.\\n116: ///\\n117: /// Data is partitioned by the value of the partitioning expression.\\n118: /// Parts belonging to different partitions are not merged - for the ease of administration (data sync and backup).\\n119: ///\\n120: /// File structure of old-style month-partitioned tables (format_version = 0):\\n121: /// Part directory - / min-date _ max-date _ min-id _ max-id _ level /\\n122: /// Inside the part directory:\\n123: /// checksums.txt - contains the list of all files along with their sizes and checksums.\\n124: /// columns.txt - contains the list of all columns and their types.\\n125: /// primary.idx - contains the primary index.\\n126: /// [Column].bin - contains compressed column data.\\n127: /// [Column].mrk - marks, pointing to seek positions allowing to skip n * k rows.\\n128: ///\\n129: /// File structure of tables with custom partitioning (format_version >= 1):\\n130: /// Part directory - / partition-id _ min-id _ max-id _ level /\\n131: /// Inside the part directory:\\n132: /// The same files as for month-partitioned tables, plus\\n133: /// count.txt - contains total number of rows in this part.\\n134: /// partition.dat - contains the value of the partitioning expression.\\n135: /// minmax_[Column].idx - MinMax indexes (see IMergeTreeDataPart::MinMaxIndex class) for the columns required by the partitioning expression.\\n136: ///\\n137: /// Several modes are implemented. Modes determine additional actions during merge:\\n138: /// - Ordinary - don't do anything special\\n139: /// - Collapsing - collapse pairs of rows with the opposite values of sign_columns for the same values\\n140: ///   of primary key (cf. CollapsingSortedTransform.h)\\n141: /// - Replacing - for all rows with the same primary key keep only the latest one. Or, if the version\\n142: ///   column is set, keep the latest row with the maximal version.\\n143: /// - Summing - sum all numeric columns not contained in the primary key for all rows with the same primary key.\\n144: /// - Aggregating - merge columns containing aggregate function states for all rows with the same primary key.\\n145: /// - Graphite - performs coarsening of historical data for Graphite (a system for quantitative monitoring).\\n146: \\n147: /// The MergeTreeData class contains a list of parts and the data structure parameters.\\n148: /// To read and modify the data use other High-Level Architecture\n\n```\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│                      ClickHouse Server                          │\n│                                                                 │\n│  ┌──────────┐   ┌──────────────────┐   ┌─────────────────────┐ │\n│  │  INSERT   │   │     SELECT       │   │  Background Worker  │ │\n│  └────┬─────┘   └────────┬─────────┘   └──────────┬──────────┘ │\n│       │                  │                         │            │\n│       ▼                  ▼                         ▼            │\n│  ┌──────────┐   ┌──────────────────┐   ┌─────────────────────┐ │\n│  │MergeTree │   │MergeTreeData     │   │MergeTreeDataMerger  │ │\n│  │   Sink   │   │SelectExecutor   │   │    Mutator          │ │\n│  └────┬─────┘   └────────┬─────────┘   └──────────┬──────────┘ │\n│       │                  │                         │            │\n│       ▼                  │                         ▼            │\n│  ┌──────────┐            │             ┌─────────────────────┐ │\n│  │MergeTree │            │             │     MergeTask       │ │\n│  │DataWriter│            │             │  (coroutine-based)  │ │\n│  └────┬─────┘            │             └──────────┬──────────┘ │\n│       │                  │                         │            │\n│       ▼                  ▼                         ▼            │\n│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │\n│  │                  MergeTreeData                          │   │\n│  │            (Central data part registry)                 │   │\n│  │  data_parts: boost::multi_index_container<DataPartPtr>  │   │\n│  └──────────────────────────┬──────────────────────────────┘   │\n│                             │                                   │\n│                             ▼                                   │\n│  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐  │\n│  │               Data Parts on Disk                         │  │\n│  │  partition_id_minBlock_maxBlock_level/                   │  │\n│  │    columns.txt   checksums.txt   primary.idx             │  │\n│  │    [col].bin     [col].mrk2      [idx].idx               │  │\n│  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘  │\n└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n## 2. Data Part Structure\n\nA data part is the fundamental unit of storage in MergeTree. Each INSERT creates one or more parts; background merges combine multiple parts into one.\n\n### Part Directory Naming Convention\n\n```\n{partition_id}_{min_block}_{max_block}_{level}[_{mutation}]/\n```\n\n- **partition_id**: hash or value of the partition expression\n- **min_block / max_block**: monotonically-increasing block numbers covering the inserted range\n- **level**: merge depth (0 = freshly inserted, increments with each merge)\n- **mutation**: mutation version (appended after mutations)\n\nExamples: `all_1_1_0`, `all_1_3_1`, `20240101_5_10_2_42`\n\n**Source**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreePartInfo.h` — `struct MergeTreePartInfo`\n\n### Files Inside a Data Part (Wide Format)\n\n```\n<part_dir>/\n├── columns.txt          — list of columns and their data types\n├── checksums.txt        — file sizes and SHA256 checksums for data integrity\n├── count.txt            — total number of rows\n├── primary.idx          — sparse primary key index (one entry per granule)\n├── partition.dat        — serialized partition key value\n├── minmax_<col>.idx     — min/max index per column in the partition key\n├── <column>.bin         — compressed column data (LZ4 / ZSTD)\n├── <column>.mrk2        — mark file: (compressed_offset, uncompressed_offset) per granule\n├── skp_idx_<name>.idx   — data-skipping (secondary) index data\n├── skp_idx_<name>.mrk2  — mark file for the skip index\n└── metadata_version.txt — schema metadata version\n```\n\nFor **Compact** format (small parts), all columns are stored in a single `data.bin` / `data.mrk2` file pair.\n\n**Source**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeData.h` (lines 120–135 comments), `src/Storages/MergeTree/IMergeTreeDataPart.h`\n\n### Part Types\n\n| Type    | Layout                                       | When used                          |\n|---------|----------------------------------------------|------------------------------------|\n| Wide    | One `.bin` + `.mrk2` per column              | Large parts (many rows/bytes)      |\n| Compact | Single `data.bin` + `data.mrk2`              | Small parts (fresh inserts)        |\n\n**Source**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartWide.h`, `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartCompact.h`\n\n### Index Granularity\n\nThe primary index is **sparse** — one index entry is stored for every `index_granularity` rows (default: 8192). Each granule corresponds to a mark in the `.mrk2` file, which records byte offsets into the `.bin` file.\n\n**Source**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexGranularity.h`, `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexGranularityInfo.h`\n\n### Part Lifecycle (State Machine)\n\n```\nTemporary → PreActive → Active → Outdated → Deleting → (deleted)\n                ↓\n            Outdated  (rollback)\n```\n\n**Source**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartState.h`\n\n---\n\n## 3. Write Path: INSERT to Committed Part\n\n### Flow Diagram\n\n```\nINSERT statement\n      │\n      ▼\nMergeTreeSink::consume()          [src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeSink.cpp]\n      │\n      ├─ splitBlockIntoParts()    — splits block by partition key\n      │     [MergeTreeDataWriter.cpp]\n      │\n      ├─ writeTempPart()          — creates a temporary part\n      │     [MergeTreeDataWriter.cpp]\n      │     │\n      │     ├─ Evaluate partition key expression\n      │     ├─ Build MinMaxIndex (per-part min/max for partitioning columns)\n      │     ├─ Evaluate sorting key expression\n      │     ├─ Sort rows by primary key (stableGetPermutation)\n      │     ├─ Optionally apply merging algorithm (ReplacingMT, SummingMT, etc.)\n      │     ├─ Write column data → <col>.bin\n      │     ├─ Write marks      → <col>.mrk2\n      │     ├─ Write primary.idx (one entry per granule)\n      │     └─ Write skip index files (if materialize_skip_indexes_on_insert=1)\n      │\n      └─ finishDelayedChunk()\n            │\n            ├─ temp_part.finalize()         — flush + fsync\n            ├─ lockParts()\n            ├─ renameTempPartAndAdd()       — rename tmp_insert_XXX → final name\n            ├─ transaction.commit()         — part state: PreActive → Active\n            └─ background_operations_assignee.trigger()  — wake up merger\n```\n\n### Key Details\n\n1. **Block splitting** (`MergeTreeDataWriter::splitBlockIntoParts`): The incoming block is hashed on partition key columns and scattered into per-partition sub-blocks.\n\n2. **Sorting** (`writeTempPartImpl`): Rows are sorted in-memory by the primary/sorting key using a stable permutation. If `optimize_row_order=true`, an additional row-order optimisation is applied.\n\n3. **Merging on insert**: For specialised engines (ReplacingMergeTree, SummingMergeTree, etc.), `mergeBlock()` runs the appropriate `IMergingAlgorithm` on the single sorted block before writing.\n\n4. **Part naming**: `MergeTreePartInfo::getPartNameV1()` produces the final name `{partition}_{min}_{max}_{level}`. While writing, the directory is prefixed with `tmp_insert_`.\n\n5. **Transaction commit**: `MergeTreeData::Transaction::commit()` atomically moves the part from `PreActive` to `Active` in the in-memory set, making it visible to `SELECT` queries.\n\n**Key source files**:\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeSink.cpp` — consume/finalize pipeline\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataWriter.cpp` — core write logic\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergedBlockOutputStream.cpp` — streaming column writer\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartWriterWide.cpp` — Wide format column writer\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartWriterCompact.cpp` — Compact format writer\n\n---\n\n## 4. Merge Path: Background Merges\n\n### Overview\n\nBackground merges are triggered by `BackgroundJobsAssignee` immediately after a successful INSERT. The merge process reduces part count, reclaims space (via TTL / deduplication), and keeps query performance high.\n\n### Flow Diagram\n\n```\nBackgroundJobsAssignee::trigger()         [BackgroundJobsAssignee.cpp]\n      │\n      ▼\nMergePlainMergeTreeTask::executeStep()    [MergePlainMergeTreeTask.cpp]\n      │\n      ▼\nMergeTreeDataMergerMutator::selectPartsToMerge()\n      │                              [MergeTreeDataMergerMutator.cpp]\n      ├─ Step 1: getDataPartsToSelectMergeFrom()\n      │     — collect all Active parts (respecting transactions)\n      │\n      ├─ Step 2: getPossibleMergeRanges()\n      │     — split parts into contiguous mergeable ranges using\n      │       can_merge_callback (no gaps allowed between blocks)\n      │\n      └─ Step 3: selectPartsToMergeFromRanges()\n            — apply SimpleMergeSelector / TTLMergeSelector heuristics\n              (balance part sizes, prefer newer partitions, respect\n               max_bytes_to_merge_at_max_space_in_pool setting)\n      │\n      ▼\nMergeTask (coroutine)                     [MergeTask.cpp / MergeTask.h]\n      │\n      ├─ Stage 1: ExecuteAndFinalizeHorizontalPart\n      │     ├─ Open MergeTreeSequentialSource on each source part\n      │     ├─ Feed streams into MergingSortedTransform (k-way merge sort)\n      │     │   (or ReplacingSorted / CollapsingSorted / SummingSorted etc.)\n      │     ├─ Write merged blocks via MergedBlockOutputStream\n      │     │     → new <col>.bin, <col>.mrk2, primary.idx\n      │     └─ Suspends between blocks (coroutine yield)\n      │\n      ├─ Stage 2: MergeVerticalStage (for Wide parts with many columns)\n      │     — re-reads remaining columns and writes them independently,\n      │       using ColumnGathererTransform guided by the row sources\n      │       file produced in Stage 1\n      │\n      └─ Stage 3: MergeProjectionStage\n            — re-materialise each projection defined on the table\n      │\n      ▼\nMergeTreeData::Transaction::commit()\n      — new merged part becomes Active\n      — source parts become Outdated → eventually Deleting → removed\n```\n\n### Merge Selection Heuristics\n\n`SimpleMergeSelector` (the default) uses a score-based algorithm:\n- Prefers merging parts of similar sizes (exponential base factor).\n- Respects `max_bytes_to_merge_at_max_space_in_pool` / `max_bytes_to_merge_at_min_space_in_pool` thresholds (interpolated based on pool saturation).\n- `TTLMergeSelector` is invoked instead when TTL-expired parts need compaction.\n\n**Key source files**:\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataMergerMutator.cpp` — part selection logic\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTask.cpp` — merge coroutine implementation\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeSelectors/SimpleMergeSelector.cpp` — scoring algorithm\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeSelectors/TTLMergeSelector.cpp` — TTL-aware selector\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergedBlockOutputStream.cpp` — merged output writer\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/FutureMergedMutatedPart.h` — represents the planned new part\n\n---\n\n## 5. Read Path: SELECT with Index Skipping\n\n### Flow Diagram\n\n```\nSELECT query\n      │\n      ▼\nMergeTreeDataSelectExecutor::read()\n      │                          [MergeTreeDataSelectExecutor.cpp]\n      ├─ Acquire snapshot: list of Active DataParts at query start\n      │\n      ├─ Partition pruning (PartitionPruner)\n      │     — evaluate partition key condition against part's\n      │       minmax_<col>.idx → skip entire partitions\n      │     [PartitionPruner.cpp]\n      │\n      ├─ Per-part primary key scan (markRangesFromPKRange)\n      │     — binary search on primary.idx loaded into memory\n      │     — produces MarkRanges: list of [begin_mark, end_mark) intervals\n      │     — coarse (8×index_granularity) then fine granularity scan\n      │\n      ├─ Skip index filtering (filterMarksUsingIndex)\n      │     — for each secondary index (bloom filter, minmax, set, etc.)\n      │       read the .idx file and eliminate mark ranges that cannot\n      │       contain matching rows\n      │     [MergeTreeIndexReader.cpp, MergeTreeIndices.h]\n      │\n      ├─ Build ReadFromMergeTree query plan step\n      │     — distributes RangesInDataPart across N threads via\n      │       MergeTreeReadPool / MergeTreePrefetchedReadPool\n      │     [ReadFromMergeTree.cpp, MergeTreeReadPool.cpp]\n      │\n      └─ Per-thread MergeTreeSelectProcessor\n            │                      [MergeTreeSelectProcessor.cpp]\n            └─ MergeTreeRangeReader\n                  — reads granule-by-granule from .bin via\n                    CompressedReadBufferFromFile\n                  — applies PREWHERE filtering before reading\n                    remaining columns (columnar short-circuit)\n                  [MergeTreeRangeReader.cpp]\n```\n\n### Key Optimizations\n\n1. **Partition pruning**: Entire partitions skipped without touching any data files, based on `minmax_<col>.idx`.\n\n2. **Primary key binary search**: The sparse primary index (`primary.idx`) is loaded into memory (or served from `PrimaryIndexCache`). A binary search over this index identifies candidate mark ranges. Only the matching granules (8192 rows each by default) are read.\n\n3. **Skip indices**: After primary-key pruning, secondary skip indices further eliminate mark ranges:\n   - **MinMax** — range condition on a column\n   - **Set** — IN-condition with a known small set\n   - **Bloom filter** — probabilistic membership test\n   - **Full-text / Gin** — inverted index for text search\n   - **Vector similarity** — ANN index for approximate nearest neighbour\n\n4. **PREWHERE optimisation** (`MergeTreeWhereOptimizer`): Heavy filter predicates are moved to PREWHERE and evaluated first on the cheapest columns, avoiding reads of other columns for non-matching rows.\n\n5. **Mark cache** (`MarkCache`): `.mrk2` files are cached in-process to avoid repeated disk seeks.\n\n6. **Parallel reading**: `MergeTreeReadPool` distributes mark ranges across multiple threads; `MergeTreePrefetchedReadPool` adds async prefetch for remote storage.\n\n**Key source files**:\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataSelectExecutor.cpp` — top-level read orchestration\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/KeyCondition.cpp` — primary key condition & binary search\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/PartitionPruner.cpp` — partition elimination\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeRangeReader.cpp` — column-at-a-time granule reader\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeReadPool.cpp` — thread work distribution\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexReader.cpp` — secondary index evaluation\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeWhereOptimizer.cpp` — PREWHERE optimisation\n\n---\n\n## 6. Key Source Files Summary\n\n| File | Role |\n|------|------|\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeData.h` | Base class for all MergeTree variants; owns the data-parts registry (`data_parts`), `MergingParams`, `Transaction` commit/rollback |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeData.cpp` | Part lifecycle management: add, remove, rename, prune; background task scheduling |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/IMergeTreeDataPart.h` | Abstract base for a data part; stores rows_count, index_granularity, MinMaxIndex, checksums, TTL info, part state |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreePartInfo.h` | `MergeTreePartInfo` struct: partition_id, min/max block, level, mutation; part containment logic |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataWriter.cpp` | `writeTempPart()`: sort, merge-on-insert, write columns/marks/primary index for a single block |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeSink.cpp` | Pipeline sink: receives chunks, calls writer, commits transaction, triggers merge |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataMergerMutator.cpp` | Three-step merge selection: collect parts → build ranges → apply selector heuristic |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTask.cpp` / `MergeTask.h` | Coroutine-based merge execution in three stages: horizontal, vertical, projections |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataSelectExecutor.cpp` | `read()` entry point: partition pruning, primary key scan, skip-index filtering, query plan construction |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/KeyCondition.cpp` | Converts WHERE/PREWHERE to a key condition; `markRangesFromPKRange()` binary-searches the primary index |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeRangeReader.cpp` | Reads mark ranges from `.bin` files column by column; implements PREWHERE short-circuit |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexGranularityInfo.h` | Fixed vs. adaptive granularity configuration; mark file extension selection |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartWriterWide.cpp` | Writes one `.bin`/`.mrk2` pair per column in Wide format; computes marks per granule |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergedBlockOutputStream.cpp` | High-level merge output stream used by both merges and mutations |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartState.h` | State machine enum: Temporary → PreActive → Active → Outdated → Deleting |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/PartitionPruner.cpp` | Evaluates partition condition against part min/max; eliminates whole parts before any I/O |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeReadPool.cpp` | Distributes mark ranges across reader threads; supports in-order and parallel-replicas modes |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeSelectors/SimpleMergeSelector.cpp` | Core merge heuristic: scores part ranges by size balance and age |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/BackgroundJobsAssignee.cpp` | Schedules merges/mutations/moves on the background thread pool |\n\n---\n\n## 7. MergeTree Engine Variants\n\nThe `MergeTreeData::MergingParams::Mode` enum selects additional processing applied during both insert-time `mergeBlock()` and background merges:\n\n| Mode | Engine | Merge Behaviour |\n|------|--------|----------------|\n| `Ordinary` (0) | MergeTree | No deduplication; rows are preserved as-is |\n| `Collapsing` (1) | CollapsingMergeTree | Cancel pairs of rows with opposite `sign` column values |\n| `Summing` (2) | SummingMergeTree | Sum numeric columns for identical primary key rows |\n| `Aggregating` (3) | AggregatingMergeTree | Merge aggregate function states |\n| `Replacing` (5) | ReplacingMergeTree | Keep only the latest version of each primary key |\n| `Graphite` (6) | GraphiteMergeTree | Time-series rollup for Graphite metrics |\n| `VersionedCollapsing` (7) | VersionedCollapsingMergeTree | Version-aware collapse with sign column |\n\n**Source**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeData.h` (lines 339–351)\n\n---\n\n## 8. Replication Layer\n\nFor `ReplicatedMergeTree`, all merges and mutations are coordinated via ZooKeeper:\n- Each replica maintains a `/replicas/<name>/queue` of log entries.\n- `ReplicatedMergeTreeQueue` (`src/Storages/MergeTree/ReplicatedMergeTreeQueue.cpp`) applies entries (merges, mutations, fetches) in order.\n- `MergeFromLogEntryTask` and `MutateFromLogEntryTask` wrap `MergeTask` / `MutateTask`.\n- Part replication between replicas uses `DataPartsExchange` (`src/Storages/MergeTree/DataPartsExchange.cpp`).\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":5828,"cache_read_input_tokens":63187,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":5828,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":9,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"cd2cf39c-50a7-41e3-b6ec-bc87789161af","uuid":"873b2253-0541-4bc2-82b6-f7bda40480b9"}

High-Level Architecture\n\n```\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│                      ClickHouse Server                          │\n│                                                                 │\n│  ┌──────────┐   ┌──────────────────┐   ┌─────────────────────┐ │\n│  │  INSERT   │   │     SELECT       │   │  Background Worker  │ │\n│  └────┬─────┘   └────────┬─────────┘   └──────────┬──────────┘ │\n│       │                  │                         │            │\n│       ▼                  ▼                         ▼            │\n│  ┌──────────┐   ┌──────────────────┐   ┌─────────────────────┐ │\n│  │MergeTree │   │MergeTreeData     │   │MergeTreeDataMerger  │ │\n│  │   Sink   │   │SelectExecutor    │   │    Mutator          │ │\n│  └────┬─────┘   └────────┬─────────┘   └──────────┬──────────┘ │\n│       │                  │                         │            │\n│       ▼                  │                         ▼            │\n│  ┌──────────┐            │             ┌─────────────────────┐ │\n│  │MergeTree │            │             │     MergeTask       │ │\n│  │DataWriter│            │             │  (coroutine-based)  │ │\n│  └────┬─────┘            │             └──────────┬──────────┘ │\n│       │                  │                         │            │\n│       ▼                  ▼                         ▼            │\n│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │\n│  │                  MergeTreeData                          │   │\n│  │            (Central data part registry)                 │   │\n│  │  data_parts: boost::multi_index_container<DataPartPtr>  │   │\n│  └──────────────────────────┬──────────────────────────────┘   │\n│                             │                                   │\n│                             ▼                                   │\n│  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐  │\n│  │               Data Parts on Disk                         │  │\n│  │  partition_id_minBlock_maxBlock_level/                   │  │\n│  │    columns.txt   checksums.txt   primary.idx             │  │\n│  │    [col].bin     [col].mrk2      [idx].idx               │  │\n│  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘  │\n└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n## 2. Data Part Structure\n\nA data part is the fundamental unit of storage in MergeTree. Each INSERT creates one or more parts; background merges combine multiple parts into one.\n\n### Part Directory Naming Convention\n\n```\n{partition_id}_{min_block}_{max_block}_{level}[_{mutation}]/\n```\n\n- **partition_id**: hash or value of the partition expression\n- **min_block / max_block**: monotonically-increasing block numbers covering the inserted range\n- **level**: merge depth (0 = freshly inserted, increments with each merge)\n- **mutation**: mutation version (appended after mutations)\n\nExamples: `all_1_1_0`, `all_1_3_1`, `20240101_5_10_2_42`\n\n**Source**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreePartInfo.h` — `struct MergeTreePartInfo`\n\n### Files Inside a Data Part (Wide Format)\n\n```\n<part_dir>/\n├── columns.txt          — list of columns and their data types\n├── checksums.txt        — file sizes and SHA256 checksums for data integrity\n├── count.txt            — total number of rows\n├── primary.idx          — sparse primary key index (one entry per granule)\n├── partition.dat        — serialized partition key value\n├── minmax_<col>.idx     — min/max index per column in the partition key\n├── <column>.bin         — compressed column data (LZ4 / ZSTD)\n├── <column>.mrk2        — mark file: (compressed_offset, uncompressed_offset) per granule\n├── skp_idx_<name>.idx   — data-skipping (secondary) index data\n├── skp_idx_<name>.mrk2  — mark file for the skip index\n└── metadata_version.txt — schema metadata version\n```\n\nFor **Compact** format (small parts), all columns are stored in a single `data.bin` / `data.mrk2` file pair.\n\n**Source**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeData.h` (lines 120–135 comments), `src/Storages/MergeTree/IMergeTreeDataPart.h`\n\n### Part Format Types\n\n| Type    | Layout                                  | When used                     |\n|---------|-----------------------------------------|-------------------------------|\n| Wide    | One `.bin` + `.mrk2` per column         | Large parts (many rows/bytes) |\n| Compact | Single `data.bin` + `data.mrk2`         | Small parts (fresh inserts)   |\n\n**Source**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartWide.h`, `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartCompact.h`\n\n### Index Granularity\n\nThe primary index is **sparse** — one index entry is stored for every `index_granularity` rows (default: 8192). Each granule corresponds to a mark in the `.mrk2` file, which records byte offsets into the `.bin` file for efficient random seeks.\n\n**Source**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexGranularity.h`, `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexGranularityInfo.h`\n\n### Part Lifecycle (State Machine)\n\n```\nTemporary → PreActive → Active → Outdated → Deleting → (deleted)\n                ↓\n            Outdated  (rollback on failure)\n```\n\n**Source**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartState.h`\n\n---\n\n## 3. Write Path: INSERT to Committed Part\n\n### Flow Diagram\n\n```\nINSERT statement\n      │\n      ▼\nMergeTreeSink::consume()          [src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeSink.cpp]\n      │\n      ├─ splitBlockIntoParts()    — split block by partition key into sub-blocks\n      │     [MergeTreeDataWriter.cpp]\n      │\n      ├─ writeTempPart()          — create a temporary part per partition\n      │     [MergeTreeDataWriter.cpp]\n      │     │\n      │     ├─ Evaluate partition key expression\n      │     ├─ Build MinMaxIndex (per-part min/max for partitioning columns)\n      │     ├─ Evaluate sorting key expression\n      │     ├─ Sort rows by primary key (stableGetPermutation)\n      │     ├─ Optionally apply merging algorithm (Replacing, Summing, etc.)\n      │     ├─ Write column data    → <col>.bin\n      │     ├─ Write mark file      → <col>.mrk2\n      │     ├─ Write primary.idx    (one entry per granule)\n      │     └─ Write skip index files (if materialize_skip_indexes_on_insert=1)\n      │\n      └─ finishDelayedChunk()\n            │\n            ├─ temp_part.finalize()         — flush buffers + optional fsync\n            ├─ lockParts()\n            ├─ renameTempPartAndAdd()       — rename tmp_insert_XXX → final name\n            ├─ transaction.commit()         — part state: PreActive → Active\n            └─ background_operations_assignee.trigger()  — wake up merger\n```\n\n### Key Details\n\n1. **Block splitting** (`MergeTreeDataWriter::splitBlockIntoParts`): The incoming block is hashed on partition key columns using `buildScatterSelector()` and scattered into per-partition sub-blocks.\n\n2. **Sorting** (`writeTempPartImpl`): Rows are sorted in-memory by the primary/sorting key using a stable permutation. If `optimize_row_order=true`, an additional row-order optimization (Hilbert curve locality) is applied.\n\n3. **Merging on insert**: For specialised engines (ReplacingMergeTree, SummingMergeTree, etc.), `mergeBlock()` runs the appropriate `IMergingAlgorithm` on the single sorted block before writing, pre-collapsing redundant rows.\n\n4. **Part naming**: `MergeTreePartInfo::getPartNameV1()` produces the final name `{partition}_{min}_{max}_{level}`. While writing, the directory is prefixed with `tmp_insert_`.\n\n5. **Transaction commit**: `MergeTreeData::Transaction::commit()` atomically moves the part from `PreActive` to `Active` in the in-memory `data_parts` set, making it immediately visible to `SELECT` queries.\n\n**Key source files**:\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeSink.cpp` — consume/finalize pipeline\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataWriter.cpp` — core write logic (sorting, block splitting, temp part creation)\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergedBlockOutputStream.cpp` — streaming column writer used during write\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartWriterWide.cpp` — Wide format column writer (per-column streams)\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartWriterCompact.cpp` — Compact format writer (single stream)\n\n---\n\n## 4. Merge Path: Background Merges\n\n### Overview\n\nBackground merges are triggered by `BackgroundJobsAssignee` after successful INSERTs. The merge process reduces part count, reclaims space via TTL / deduplication, and keeps read performance high by consolidating small parts.\n\n### Flow Diagram\n\n```\nBackgroundJobsAssignee::trigger()         [BackgroundJobsAssignee.cpp]\n      │\n      ▼\nMergePlainMergeTreeTask::executeStep()    [MergePlainMergeTreeTask.cpp]\n      │\n      ▼\nMergeTreeDataMergerMutator::selectPartsToMerge()\n      │                              [MergeTreeDataMergerMutator.cpp]\n      ├─ Step 1: getDataPartsToSelectMergeFrom()\n      │     — collect all Active parts (respecting transactions)\n      │\n      ├─ Step 2: getPossibleMergeRanges()\n      │     — split parts into contiguous mergeable ranges using\n      │       can_merge_callback (no inter-part gaps allowed within range)\n      │\n      └─ Step 3: selectPartsToMergeFromRanges()\n            — apply SimpleMergeSelector / TTLMergeSelector heuristics\n              (balance part sizes, respect max_bytes_to_merge_at_max_space_in_pool)\n      │\n      ▼\nMergeTask (coroutine)                     [MergeTask.cpp / MergeTask.h]\n      │\n      ├─ Stage 1: ExecuteAndFinalizeHorizontalPart\n      │     ├─ Open MergeTreeSequentialSource on each source part\n      │     ├─ Feed streams into MergingSortedTransform (k-way merge sort)\n      │     │   (or ReplacingSorted / CollapsingSorted / SummingSorted etc.)\n      │     ├─ Write merged blocks via MergedBlockOutputStream\n      │     │     → new <col>.bin, <col>.mrk2, primary.idx\n      │     └─ Suspends between blocks (coroutine yield for cooperative scheduling)\n      │\n      ├─ Stage 2: MergeVerticalStage (for Wide parts with many columns)\n      │     — re-reads remaining columns independently using ColumnGathererTransform\n      │       guided by the row-sources file produced in Stage 1\n      │\n      └─ Stage 3: MergeProjectionStage\n            — re-materialise each projection defined on the table\n      │\n      ▼\nMergeTreeData::Transaction::commit()\n      — new merged part becomes Active\n      — source parts become Outdated → eventually Deleting → removed from disk\n```\n\n### Merge Selection Heuristics\n\n`SimpleMergeSelector` (the default) uses a score-based algorithm:\n- Prefers merging parts of similar sizes (configurable exponential base factor via `merge_selector_base`).\n- Respects `max_bytes_to_merge_at_max_space_in_pool` / `max_bytes_to_merge_at_min_space_in_pool` thresholds, interpolated based on background pool saturation.\n- `TTLMergeSelector` is invoked instead when TTL-expired parts need compaction.\n- Pool entries are tracked via `CurrentMetrics::BackgroundMergesAndMutationsPoolTask`.\n\n**Key source files**:\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataMergerMutator.cpp` — three-step part selection logic\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTask.cpp` / `MergeTask.h` — merge coroutine (three stages)\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeSelectors/SimpleMergeSelector.cpp` — scoring algorithm\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeSelectors/TTLMergeSelector.cpp` — TTL-aware selector\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergedBlockOutputStream.cpp` — merged output writer\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/FutureMergedMutatedPart.h` — descriptor of the planned new part\n\n---\n\n## 5. Read Path: SELECT with Index Skipping\n\n### Flow Diagram\n\n```\nSELECT query\n      │\n      ▼\nMergeTreeDataSelectExecutor::read()\n      │                          [MergeTreeDataSelectExecutor.cpp]\n      ├─ Acquire snapshot of Active DataParts at query start\n      │\n      ├─ Partition pruning (PartitionPruner)\n      │     — evaluate partition key condition against each part's\n      │       minmax_<col>.idx → skip entire partitions without I/O\n      │     [src/Storages/MergeTree/PartitionPruner.cpp]\n      │\n      ├─ Per-part primary key scan (markRangesFromPKRange)\n      │     — load primary.idx into memory (or serve from PrimaryIndexCache)\n      │     — binary search produces MarkRanges: [begin_mark, end_mark) intervals\n      │     — coarse pass (merge_tree_coarse_index_granularity × granule_size)\n      │       then fine pass at granule resolution\n      │     [src/Storages/MergeTree/KeyCondition.cpp]\n      │\n      ├─ Skip index filtering (filterMarksUsingIndex)\n      │     — for each secondary index (bloom filter, minmax, set, etc.)\n      │       read the .idx file, evaluate condition, eliminate non-matching\n      │       mark ranges before any column data is read\n      │     [src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexReader.cpp]\n      │\n      ├─ Build ReadFromMergeTree query plan step\n      │     — distributes RangesInDataPart across N reader threads via\n      │       MergeTreeReadPool / MergeTreePrefetchedReadPool\n      │     [src/Processors/QueryPlan/ReadFromMergeTree.cpp]\n      │     [src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeReadPool.cpp]\n      │\n      └─ Per-thread MergeTreeSelectProcessor\n            │                      [src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeSelectProcessor.cpp]\n            └─ MergeTreeRangeReader\n                  — reads granule-by-granule from .bin via\n                    CompressedReadBufferFromFile, seeking to marks in .mrk2\n                  — applies PREWHERE filtering before reading remaining columns\n                    (columnar short-circuit: unread columns save I/O)\n                  [src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeRangeReader.cpp]\n```\n\n### Key Optimizations\n\n1. **Partition pruning**: Entire partitions are skipped without touching any column data files, based on `minmax_<col>.idx` stored per part.\n\n2. **Primary key binary search**: The sparse primary index (`primary.idx`) is loaded into memory (or served from `PrimaryIndexCache`). Binary search over this index identifies candidate mark ranges. Only the matching granules (8192 rows each by default) are read from disk.\n\n3. **Skip indices**: After primary-key pruning, secondary skip indices further eliminate mark ranges before any column data is read:\n   - **MinMax** — range condition on a column (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexMinMax.cpp`)\n   - **Set** — IN-condition with a known small set (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexSet.cpp`)\n   - **Bloom filter** — probabilistic membership test (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexBloomFilter.cpp`)\n   - **Full-text / Gin** — inverted index for text search (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexFullText.cpp`)\n   - **Vector similarity** — ANN index for approximate nearest-neighbour (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexVectorSimilarity.cpp`)\n\n4. **PREWHERE optimisation** (`MergeTreeWhereOptimizer`): Heavy filter predicates are moved to PREWHERE and evaluated first on the cheapest/smallest columns, avoiding reads of other columns for non-matching rows.\n\n5. **Mark cache** (`MarkCache`): `.mrk2` files are cached in-process to avoid repeated disk seeks on repeated queries.\n\n6. **Parallel reading**: `MergeTreeReadPool` distributes mark ranges across multiple threads; `MergeTreePrefetchedReadPool` (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreePrefetchedReadPool.cpp`) adds async prefetch for remote (S3/HDFS) storage.\n\n**Key source files**:\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataSelectExecutor.cpp` — top-level read orchestration\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/KeyCondition.cpp` — primary key condition & binary search (`markRangesFromPKRange`)\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/PartitionPruner.cpp` — partition elimination\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeRangeReader.cpp` — column-at-a-time granule reader with PREWHERE\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeReadPool.cpp` — thread work distribution\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexReader.cpp` — secondary index evaluation\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeWhereOptimizer.cpp` — PREWHERE optimisation\n\n---\n\n## 6. Key Source Files Summary\n\n| File | Role |\n|------|------|\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeData.h` | Base class for all MergeTree variants; owns the `data_parts` registry, `MergingParams`, `Transaction` commit/rollback |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeData.cpp` | Part lifecycle management: add, remove, rename, prune; background task scheduling |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/IMergeTreeDataPart.h` | Abstract base for a data part; stores rows_count, index_granularity, MinMaxIndex, checksums, TTL info, part state |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreePartInfo.h` | `MergeTreePartInfo` struct: partition_id, min/max block, level, mutation; part containment / disjointness logic |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartState.h` | State machine enum: Temporary → PreActive → Active → Outdated → Deleting |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataWriter.cpp` | `writeTempPart()`: sort, merge-on-insert, write columns/marks/primary index for a single block |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeSink.cpp` | Pipeline sink: receives chunks, calls writer, commits transaction, triggers merge |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartWriterWide.cpp` | Writes one `.bin`/`.mrk2` pair per column in Wide format; computes marks per granule |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartWriterCompact.cpp` | Writes all columns into a single `data.bin`/`data.mrk2` for Compact format |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergedBlockOutputStream.cpp` | High-level merge output stream used by both merges and mutations |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataMergerMutator.cpp` | Three-step merge selection: collect parts → build ranges → apply selector heuristic |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTask.cpp` | Coroutine-based merge execution in three stages: horizontal, vertical, projections |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTask.h` | MergeTask interface, stage definitions, GlobalRuntimeContext |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataSelectExecutor.cpp` | `read()` entry point: partition pruning, primary key scan, skip-index filtering, query plan construction |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/KeyCondition.cpp` | Converts WHERE/PREWHERE to a key condition; `markRangesFromPKRange()` binary-searches the primary index |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/PartitionPruner.cpp` | Evaluates partition condition against part min/max; eliminates whole parts before any I/O |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeRangeReader.cpp` | Reads mark ranges from `.bin` files column by column; implements PREWHERE short-circuit |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeReadPool.cpp` | Distributes mark ranges across reader threads; supports in-order and parallel-replicas modes |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreePrefetchedReadPool.cpp` | Async prefetch read pool for remote storage (S3, HDFS) |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexReader.cpp` | Reads and evaluates secondary (skip) index files to eliminate mark ranges |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeWhereOptimizer.cpp` | Moves expensive filter conditions to PREWHERE to reduce column reads |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexGranularityInfo.h` | Fixed vs. adaptive granularity configuration; mark file extension selection |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/BackgroundJobsAssignee.cpp` | Schedules merges/mutations/moves onto the background thread pool |\n| `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeSelectors/SimpleMergeSelector.cpp` | Core merge heuristic: scores part ranges by size balance and part age |\n\n---\n\n## 7. Replication Layer\n\nFor `ReplicatedMergeTree`, all merges and mutations are coordinated via ZooKeeper:\n- Each replica maintains a `/replicas/<name>/queue` of log entries.\n- `ReplicatedMergeTreeQueue` (`src/Storages/MergeTree/ReplicatedMergeTreeQueue.cpp`) applies entries (merges, mutations, fetches) in order.\n- `MergeFromLogEntryTask` (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeFromLogEntryTask.cpp`) and `MutateFromLogEntryTask` wrap `MergeTask` / `MutateTask`.\n- Part replication between replicas uses `DataPartsExchange` (`src/Storages/MergeTree/DataPartsExchange.cpp`).\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":3,"cache_creation_input_tokens":374,"cache_read_input_tokens":75137,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":374,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"cd2cf39c-50a7-41e3-b6ec-bc87789161af","uuid":"8b687d98-6bb8-4d17-80ca-33d6d31159a5"}

High-Level Architecture\n\n```\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│                      ClickHouse Server                          │\n│                                                                 │\n│  ┌──────────┐   ┌──────────────────┐   ┌─────────────────────┐ │\n│  │  INSERT   │   │     SELECT       │   │  Background Worker  │ │\n│  └────┬─────┘   └────────┬─────────┘   └──────────┬──────────┘ │\n│       │                  │                         │            │\n│       ▼                  ▼                         ▼            │\n│  ┌──────────┐   ┌──────────────────┐   ┌─────────────────────┐ │\n│  │MergeTree │   │MergeTreeData     │   │MergeTreeDataMerger  │ │\n│  │   Sink   │   │SelectExecutor    │   │    Mutator          │ │\n│  └────┬─────┘   └────────┬─────────┘   └──────────┬──────────┘ │\n│       │                  │                         │            │\n│       ▼                  │                         ▼            │\n│  ┌──────────┐            │             ┌─────────────────────┐ │\n│  │MergeTree │            │             │     MergeTask       │ │\n│  │DataWriter│            │             │  (coroutine-based)  │ │\n│  └────┬─────┘            │             └──────────┬──────────┘ │\n│       │                  │                         │            │\n│       ▼                  ▼                         ▼            │\n│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │\n│  │                  MergeTreeData                          │   │\n│  │            (Central data part registry)                 │   │\n│  │  data_parts: boost::multi_index_container<DataPartPtr>  │   │\n│  └──────────────────────────┬──────────────────────────────┘   │\n│                             │                                   │\n│                             ▼                                   │\n│  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐  │\n│  │               Data Parts on Disk                         │  │\n│  │  partition_id_minBlock_maxBlock_level/                   │  │\n│  │    columns.txt   checksums.txt   primary.idx             │  │\n│  │    [col].bin     [col].mrk2      [idx].idx               │  │\n│  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘  │\n└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n## 2. Data Part Structure\n\nA data part is the fundamental unit of storage in MergeTree. Each INSERT creates one or more parts; background merges combine multiple parts into one.\n\n### Part Directory Naming Convention\n\n```\n{partition_id}_{min_block}_{max_block}_{level}[_{mutation}]/\n```\n\n- **partition_id**: hash or value of the partition expression\n- **min_block / max_block**: monotonically-increasing block numbers covering the inserted range\n- **level**: merge depth (0 = freshly inserted, increments with each merge)\n- **mutation**: mutation version (appended after mutations)\n\nExamples: `all_1_1_0`, `all_1_3_1`, `20240101_5_10_2_42`\n\n**Source**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreePartInfo.h` — `struct MergeTreePartInfo`\n\n### Files Inside a Data Part (Wide Format)\n\n```\n<part_dir>/\n├── columns.txt          — list of columns and their data types\n├── checksums.txt        — file sizes and SHA256 checksums for data integrity\n├── count.txt            — total number of rows\n├── primary.idx          — sparse primary key index (one entry per granule)\n├── partition.dat        — serialized partition key value\n├── minmax_<col>.idx     — min/max index per column in the partition key\n├── <column>.bin         — compressed column data (LZ4 / ZSTD)\n├── <column>.mrk2        — mark file: (compressed_offset, uncompressed_offset) per granule\n├── skp_idx_<name>.idx   — data-skipping (secondary) index data\n├── skp_idx_<name>.mrk2  — mark file for the skip index\n└── metadata_version.txt — schema metadata version\n```\n\nFor **Compact** format (small parts), all columns are stored in a single `data.bin` / `data.mrk2` file pair.\n\n**Source**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeData.h` (lines 120–135 comments), `src/Storages/MergeTree/IMergeTreeDataPart.h`\n\n### Part Format Types\n\n| Type    | Layout                                  | When used                     |\n|---------|-----------------------------------------|-------------------------------|\n| Wide    | One `.bin` + `.mrk2` per column         | Large parts (many rows/bytes) |\n| Compact | Single `data.bin` + `data.mrk2`         | Small parts (fresh inserts)   |\n\n**Source**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartWide.h`, `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartCompact.h`\n\n### Index Granularity\n\nThe primary index is **sparse** — one index entry is stored for every `index_granularity` rows (default: 8192). Each granule corresponds to a mark in the `.mrk2` file, which records byte offsets into the `.bin` file for efficient random seeks.\n\n**Source**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexGranularity.h`, `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexGranularityInfo.h`\n\n### Part Lifecycle (State Machine)\n\n```\nTemporary → PreActive → Active → Outdated → Deleting → (deleted)\n                ↓\n            Outdated  (rollback on failure)\n```\n\n**Source**: `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartState.h`\n\n---\n\n## 3. Write Path: INSERT to Committed Part\n\n### Flow Diagram\n\n```\nINSERT statement\n      │\n      ▼\nMergeTreeSink::consume()          [src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeSink.cpp]\n      │\n      ├─ splitBlockIntoParts()    — split block by partition key into sub-blocks\n      │     [MergeTreeDataWriter.cpp]\n      │\n      ├─ writeTempPart()          — create a temporary part per partition\n      │     [MergeTreeDataWriter.cpp]\n      │     │\n      │     ├─ Evaluate partition key expression\n      │     ├─ Build MinMaxIndex (per-part min/max for partitioning columns)\n      │     ├─ Evaluate sorting key expression\n      │     ├─ Sort rows by primary key (stableGetPermutation)\n      │     ├─ Optionally apply merging algorithm (Replacing, Summing, etc.)\n      │     ├─ Write column data    → <col>.bin\n      │     ├─ Write mark file      → <col>.mrk2\n      │     ├─ Write primary.idx    (one entry per granule)\n      │     └─ Write skip index files (if materialize_skip_indexes_on_insert=1)\n      │\n      └─ finishDelayedChunk()\n            │\n            ├─ temp_part.finalize()         — flush buffers + optional fsync\n            ├─ lockParts()\n            ├─ renameTempPartAndAdd()       — rename tmp_insert_XXX → final name\n            ├─ transaction.commit()         — part state: PreActive → Active\n            └─ background_operations_assignee.trigger()  — wake up merger\n```\n\n### Key Details\n\n1. **Block splitting** (`MergeTreeDataWriter::splitBlockIntoParts`): The incoming block is hashed on partition key columns using `buildScatterSelector()` and scattered into per-partition sub-blocks.\n\n2. **Sorting** (`writeTempPartImpl`): Rows are sorted in-memory by the primary/sorting key using a stable permutation. If `optimize_row_order=true`, an additional row-order optimization (Hilbert curve locality) is applied.\n\n3. **Merging on insert**: For specialised engines (ReplacingMergeTree, SummingMergeTree, etc.), `mergeBlock()` runs the appropriate `IMergingAlgorithm` on the single sorted block before writing, pre-collapsing redundant rows.\n\n4. **Part naming**: `MergeTreePartInfo::getPartNameV1()` produces the final name `{partition}_{min}_{max}_{level}`. While writing, the directory is prefixed with `tmp_insert_`.\n\n5. **Transaction commit**: `MergeTreeData::Transaction::commit()` atomically moves the part from `PreActive` to `Active` in the in-memory `data_parts` set, making it immediately visible to `SELECT` queries.\n\n**Key source files**:\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeSink.cpp` — consume/finalize pipeline\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataWriter.cpp` — core write logic (sorting, block splitting, temp part creation)\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergedBlockOutputStream.cpp` — streaming column writer used during write\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartWriterWide.cpp` — Wide format column writer (per-column streams)\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataPartWriterCompact.cpp` — Compact format writer (single stream)\n\n---\n\n## 4. Merge Path: Background Merges\n\n### Overview\n\nBackground merges are triggered by `BackgroundJobsAssignee` after successful INSERTs. The merge process reduces part count, reclaims space via TTL / deduplication, and keeps read performance high by consolidating small parts.\n\n### Flow Diagram\n\n```\nBackgroundJobsAssignee::trigger()         [BackgroundJobsAssignee.cpp]\n      │\n      ▼\nMergePlainMergeTreeTask::executeStep()    [MergePlainMergeTreeTask.cpp]\n      │\n      ▼\nMergeTreeDataMergerMutator::selectPartsToMerge()\n      │                              [MergeTreeDataMergerMutator.cpp]\n      ├─ Step 1: getDataPartsToSelectMergeFrom()\n      │     — collect all Active parts (respecting transactions)\n      │\n      ├─ Step 2: getPossibleMergeRanges()\n      │     — split parts into contiguous mergeable ranges using\n      │       can_merge_callback (no inter-part gaps allowed within range)\n      │\n      └─ Step 3: selectPartsToMergeFromRanges()\n            — apply SimpleMergeSelector / TTLMergeSelector heuristics\n              (balance part sizes, respect max_bytes_to_merge_at_max_space_in_pool)\n      │\n      ▼\nMergeTask (coroutine)                     [MergeTask.cpp / MergeTask.h]\n      │\n      ├─ Stage 1: ExecuteAndFinalizeHorizontalPart\n      │     ├─ Open MergeTreeSequentialSource on each source part\n      │     ├─ Feed streams into MergingSortedTransform (k-way merge sort)\n      │     │   (or ReplacingSorted / CollapsingSorted / SummingSorted etc.)\n      │     ├─ Write merged blocks via MergedBlockOutputStream\n      │     │     → new <col>.bin, <col>.mrk2, primary.idx\n      │     └─ Suspends between blocks (coroutine yield for cooperative scheduling)\n      │\n      ├─ Stage 2: MergeVerticalStage (for Wide parts with many columns)\n      │     — re-reads remaining columns independently using ColumnGathererTransform\n      │       guided by the row-sources file produced in Stage 1\n      │\n      └─ Stage 3: MergeProjectionStage\n            — re-materialise each projection defined on the table\n      │\n      ▼\nMergeTreeData::Transaction::commit()\n      — new merged part becomes Active\n      — source parts become Outdated → eventually Deleting → removed from disk\n```\n\n### Merge Selection Heuristics\n\n`SimpleMergeSelector` (the default) uses a score-based algorithm:\n- Prefers merging parts of similar sizes (configurable exponential base factor via `merge_selector_base`).\n- Respects `max_bytes_to_merge_at_max_space_in_pool` / `max_bytes_to_merge_at_min_space_in_pool` thresholds, interpolated based on background pool saturation.\n- `TTLMergeSelector` is invoked instead when TTL-expired parts need compaction.\n- Pool entries are tracked via `CurrentMetrics::BackgroundMergesAndMutationsPoolTask`.\n\n**Key source files**:\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataMergerMutator.cpp` — three-step part selection logic\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTask.cpp` / `MergeTask.h` — merge coroutine (three stages)\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeSelectors/SimpleMergeSelector.cpp` — scoring algorithm\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeSelectors/TTLMergeSelector.cpp` — TTL-aware selector\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergedBlockOutputStream.cpp` — merged output writer\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/FutureMergedMutatedPart.h` — descriptor of the planned new part\n\n---\n\n## 5. Read Path: SELECT with Index Skipping\n\n### Flow Diagram\n\n```\nSELECT query\n      │\n      ▼\nMergeTreeDataSelectExecutor::read()\n      │                          [MergeTreeDataSelectExecutor.cpp]\n      ├─ Acquire snapshot of Active DataParts at query start\n      │\n      ├─ Partition pruning (PartitionPruner)\n      │     — evaluate partition key condition against each part's\n      │       minmax_<col>.idx → skip entire partitions without I/O\n      │     [src/Storages/MergeTree/PartitionPruner.cpp]\n      │\n      ├─ Per-part primary key scan (markRangesFromPKRange)\n      │     — load primary.idx into memory (or serve from PrimaryIndexCache)\n      │     — binary search produces MarkRanges: [begin_mark, end_mark) intervals\n      │     — coarse pass (merge_tree_coarse_index_granularity × granule_size)\n      │       then fine pass at granule resolution\n      │     [src/Storages/MergeTree/KeyCondition.cpp]\n      │\n      ├─ Skip index filtering (filterMarksUsingIndex)\n      │     — for each secondary index (bloom filter, minmax, set, etc.)\n      │       read the .idx file, evaluate condition, eliminate non-matching\n      │       mark ranges before any column data is read\n      │     [src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexReader.cpp]\n      │\n      ├─ Build ReadFromMergeTree query plan step\n      │     — distributes RangesInDataPart across N reader threads via\n      │       MergeTreeReadPool / MergeTreePrefetchedReadPool\n      │     [src/Processors/QueryPlan/ReadFromMergeTree.cpp]\n      │     [src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeReadPool.cpp]\n      │\n      └─ Per-thread MergeTreeSelectProcessor\n            │                      [src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeSelectProcessor.cpp]\n            └─ MergeTreeRangeReader\n                  — reads granule-by-granule from .bin via\n                    CompressedReadBufferFromFile, seeking to marks in .mrk2\n                  — applies PREWHERE filtering before reading remaining columns\n                    (columnar short-circuit: unread columns save I/O)\n                  [src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeRangeReader.cpp]\n```\n\n### Key Optimizations\n\n1. **Partition pruning**: Entire partitions are skipped without touching any column data files, based on `minmax_<col>.idx` stored per part.\n\n2. **Primary key binary search**: The sparse primary index (`primary.idx`) is loaded into memory (or served from `PrimaryIndexCache`). Binary search over this index identifies candidate mark ranges. Only the matching granules (8192 rows each by default) are read from disk.\n\n3. **Skip indices**: After primary-key pruning, secondary skip indices further eliminate mark ranges before any column data is read:\n   - **MinMax** — range condition on a column (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexMinMax.cpp`)\n   - **Set** — IN-condition with a known small set (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexSet.cpp`)\n   - **Bloom filter** — probabilistic membership test (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexBloomFilter.cpp`)\n   - **Full-text / Gin** — inverted index for text search (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexFullText.cpp`)\n   - **Vector similarity** — ANN index for approximate nearest-neighbour (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexVectorSimilarity.cpp`)\n\n4. **PREWHERE optimisation** (`MergeTreeWhereOptimizer`): Heavy filter predicates are moved to PREWHERE and evaluated first on the cheapest/smallest columns, avoiding reads of other columns for non-matching rows.\n\n5. **Mark cache** (`MarkCache`): `.mrk2` files are cached in-process to avoid repeated disk seeks on repeated queries.\n\n6. **Parallel reading**: `MergeTreeReadPool` distributes mark ranges across multiple threads; `MergeTreePrefetchedReadPool` (`src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreePrefetchedReadPool.cpp`) adds async prefetch for remote (S3/HDFS) storage.\n\n**Key source files**:\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeDataSelectExecutor.cpp` — top-level read orchestration\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/KeyCondition.cpp` — primary key condition & binary search (`markRangesFromPKRange`)\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/PartitionPruner.cpp` — partition elimination\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeRangeReader.cpp` — column-at-a-time granule reader with PREWHERE\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeReadPool.cpp` — thread work distribution\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeIndexReader.cpp` — secondary index evaluation\n- `src/Storages/MergeTree/MergeTreeWhereOptimizer.cpp` — PREWHERE optimisation\n\n---\n\n## 6.
